    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2009498823" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2009498823" />
    <a title="QNPoohBear" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22177907-qnpoohbear"><img alt="QNPoohBear" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1527904848p2/22177907.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2009498823?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="QNPoohBear" class="user" itemprop="url" name="QNPoohBear" href="/user/show/22177907-qnpoohbear">QNPoohBear</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781481422123" href="/book/show/22546619-murder-is-bad-manners">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22177907-qnpoohbear?shelf=cozy-mystery">cozy-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22177907-qnpoohbear?shelf=middle-grades-historical-fiction">middle-grades-historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2009498823" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4610678198948819455">Daisy Wells and Hazel Wong are students at the Deepdean School for Girls in 1934, where nothing very interesting happens. Just in case, Daisy has formed a secret detective agency with her best friend Hazel as Watson to Daisy's Sherlock Holmes. At first the only case they solve is the mystery of Lavinia's tie but they have their eye on the teachers' love lives, specifically following their handsome art teacher, known as "The One" by his devoted students. Then Hazel discovers Science Mistress and </span>
  <span id="freeText4610678198948819455" style="display:none">Daisy Wells and Hazel Wong are students at the Deepdean School for Girls in 1934, where nothing very interesting happens. Just in case, Daisy has formed a secret detective agency with her best friend Hazel as Watson to Daisy's Sherlock Holmes. At first the only case they solve is the mystery of Lavinia's tie but they have their eye on the teachers' love lives, specifically following their handsome art teacher, known as "The One" by his devoted students. Then Hazel discovers Science Mistress and soon to be newly appointed Deputy Headmistress Miss Bell lying dead on the gymnasium floor. She runs to tell Daisy but by the time they return with an adult, the body is missing! Hazel knows what she saw was real but only Daisy believes her. Daisy and Hazel are convinced Miss Bell was pushed or fell off the balcony but who will look into the circumstances when the teachers refuse to announce Miss Bell is dead, instead clinging to a fiction that she has resigned. It sounds like a case for the Wells &amp; Wong Detective Society!<br /><br />I was expecting this novel to be more fun than it was. First, the setting is not very appealing. Boarding school works in Harry Potter because it's MAGICAL boarding school. Here it does not work. Also, there are very very few period details that would clue the reader in to the time in which the book is set. I did find the mystery engaging enough to read the whole book in one night. I figured out one of the smaller mysteries but the big whodunnit eluded me until the moment the girls discovered the truth. I was very surprised as to who and why! Why was a big shocker. I thought maybe the mystery might be more interesting if Miss Bell wasn't really dead and I wasn't expecting a second murder victim! I was also surprised at some of the language in the book. The TV would rate this TV-14 for dialogue and language. I hated the American translation of all things British. It was confusing. I didn't remember the story takes place in Britain. Read the later Harry Potter books or UK edition and you will spot the difference right away, or read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/402013.Angus__Thongs_and_Full_Frontal_Snogging__Confessions_of_Georgia_Nicolson___1_" title="Angus, Thongs and Full-Frontal Snogging (Confessions of Georgia Nicolson, #1) by Louise Rennison" rel="nofollow noopener">Angus, Thongs and Full-Frontal Snogging</a>. <br /><br />The big thing I hated about this book was the main characters. Daisy is such a queen bee. I hated her. She was cruel to Hazel when they first met and ever after Hazel was her sidekick. Even at the end after she grows up a bit, she's still selfish. It bothered me enormously that Hazel was the secretary of a society made up of only two members. Why only two? Daisy has a talent for lying so one can never be sure if she's telling the truth or not. Hazel is a more appealing character but I didn't care for her much either. A girl from a wealthy Hong Kong ethnic Chinese family she stands out among her peers. She was desperate for a friend and had dreams of what her life at an English girls' school would be like and tried to fit herself and Daisy into that vision. She clings to Daisy's friendship long after she realizes it began rather badly. Hazel is not a very strong heroine. She gives in to Daisy constantly, follows Daisy around or follows Daisy's orders. She's a follower and not a leader and I just didn't like that quality in a heroine. I did enjoy the part where she explained her background. <br /><br />I was torn between 2-3 Good Reads stars. I think somewhere closer to 3 than 2 but not a full 3. I kind of liked it but not enough to want to read more about these characters. <br /><br /><b>Content:</b><br />Discussion of canoodling -whatever that means. Canoodling between teachers (female/female, male/female, students)<br />Some language<br />blood</span>
  <a data-text-id="4610678198948819455" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_972676439" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/972676439" />
    <a title="Kribu" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5117138-kribu"><img alt="Kribu" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307111631p2/5117138.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/972676439?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kribu" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kribu" href="/user/show/5117138-kribu">Kribu</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/20946315-murder-most-unladylike">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5117138-kribu?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5117138-kribu?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5117138-kribu?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5117138-kribu?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5117138-kribu?shelf=detective">detective</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5117138-kribu?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5117138-kribu?shelf=school">school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5117138-kribu?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5117138-kribu?shelf=received-for-review">received-for-review</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer972676439" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6506284889248414558">4.5 stars. Really enjoyed this.<br/><br/>The concept of "children take it upon themselves to solve a murder" is of course hardly original, nor is the historical boarding school setting, but as with every genre story, it's all in the handling - and <i>Murder Most Unladylike</i> was, for me, handled with just the right mixture of clever plotting, amusing writing and a hint of serious issues (bullying, racism) being touched on just enough to keep the reader aware but without turning into a moralising lecture.<br/><br/>As wit</span>
  <span id="freeText6506284889248414558" style="display:none">4.5 stars. Really enjoyed this.<br /><br />The concept of "children take it upon themselves to solve a murder" is of course hardly original, nor is the historical boarding school setting, but as with every genre story, it's all in the handling - and <i>Murder Most Unladylike</i> was, for me, handled with just the right mixture of clever plotting, amusing writing and a hint of serious issues (bullying, racism) being touched on just enough to keep the reader aware but without turning into a moralising lecture.<br /><br />As with most first person books, a lot depends on the narrator's voice, and it's here that this book shined for me: the 13-year-old Hazel Wong, the Hong Kong born heroine and semi-reluctant detective, was wonderful. She felt real to me, her account of the goings-on at the boarding school both wry and mature in the sort of way that a mature 13-year-old is, capable of almost adult seriousness and awareness at times while still maintaining a youthful voice.<br /><br />I loved the little touches about her past and her first year experiences at Deepdean school, illustrating how a 1930s boarding school in England wasn't necessarily always a paradise (not the least to a foreign girl), but never making it sound too depressing, either.<br /><br />The friendship between Hazel and Daisy Wells, the blonde and blue-eyed darling of the school and President of the Detective Society (a society of two, Hazel and Daisy), also rang true to me: they're not always equal partners (if only because Daisy certainly considers herself superior - but not so much that it would have made me dislike her), but it felt a realistic description of a genuine friendship between two girls, even if one is far more popular - and a natural leader - than the other.<br /><br />The plot wasn't too shabby either: it's a children's book (or, I suppose, children's / the younger end of YA) so the mystery is relatively simple, but it came with enough twists and while I could work out some of what happened, I certainly didn't see everything coming - so for me, the balance was just right.<br /><br />As is often the case in children's books, some of the adults came off a little flat as well as caricature-ish at first, but I was glad to see several of them become rather more rounded by the end - and equally, I liked that the adults weren't depicted as utterly useless, clueless people who refuse to listen to whatever children have to say.<br /><br />Anyway, I don't often find children's mysteries I can enjoy fully, but I'm really looking forward to more cases for Hazel and Daisy to solve!<br /><br /><i>* ARC of this book was provided by the publisher through NetGalley in return for an honest review. Thanks!</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="6506284889248414558" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_891814690" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/891814690" />
    <a title="Louise / Daisy May Johnson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5230131-louise-daisy-may-johnson"><img alt="Louise / Daisy May Johnson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554735943p2/5230131.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/891814690?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Louise / Daisy May Johnson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Louise / Daisy May Johnson" href="/user/show/5230131-louise-daisy-may-johnson">Louise / Daisy May Johnson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5230131-louise-daisy-may-johnson?shelf=childrens-literature">childrens-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5230131-louise-daisy-may-johnson?shelf=school-stories">school-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5230131-louise-daisy-may-johnson?shelf=girlsown">girlsown</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer891814690" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5768866787354642701">You may know by now that I have a thing for school stories. School stories are one of the great joys of children's literature in that they do what they do so well. They tell a story in a frame which is familiar to the majority of children, and they do it with a sort of glorious constancy irrespective of date of publication. There is a part of me that wants to see Murder Most Unladylike read with books like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38977.The_Princess_of_the_Chalet_School__The_Chalet_School___3_' title='The Princess of the Chalet School (The Chalet School, #3) by Elinor M. Brent-Dyer' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Princess of the Chalet School</a> or <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7745639.Beswitched' title='Beswitched by Kate Saunders' rel='nofollow noopener'>Beswitched</a> because it fits so comfortably and solidly</span>
  <span id="freeText5768866787354642701" style="display:none">You may know by now that I have a thing for school stories. School stories are one of the great joys of children's literature in that they do what they do so well. They tell a story in a frame which is familiar to the majority of children, and they do it with a sort of glorious constancy irrespective of date of publication. There is a part of me that wants to see Murder Most Unladylike read with books like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38977.The_Princess_of_the_Chalet_School__The_Chalet_School___3_" title="The Princess of the Chalet School (The Chalet School, #3) by Elinor M. Brent-Dyer" rel="nofollow noopener">The Princess of the Chalet School</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7745639.Beswitched" title="Beswitched by Kate Saunders" rel="nofollow noopener">Beswitched</a> because it fits so comfortably and solidly into the genre. Because it is, quite possibly, the start of a very new and very lovely and very contemporary spin on the school story, despite the setting of 1930s England and tea houses and pashes. <br /><br />Murder Most Unladylike is a (Daisy) Wells and (Hazel) Wong story. It's a sort of hybrid of Angela Brazil meets Agatha Christie all mixed up with some Sherlockian tips and winks that made me snuggle down and read with a contented smile. It is a jacket potato on a winters day book; warm, satisfying, filling.<br /><br />And can I tell you what I loved most about it? What made me actually adore and fall in love with it? It is Stevens' kind and funny and lovely writing which features references to pashes and to Angela Brazil, but does it with a sort of love and respect and belief in the genre and what it can do when it's done well (which it is here, very much so). <br /><br />This is such a glorious book and it is one which has reinterpreted the school story for the contemporary reader and opened it up with a swift moving and accessible plot line. In Star Trek terms, it is the next generation as compared to the original series. It is very, very gorgeous. Daisy is glorious. Hazel is awesome. I want more, please. It's as simple as that. <br /><br />Murder Most Unladylike is published on June 5th by Random House, I would suggest we all save the date, yeah? I think that Wells and Wong are very definitely worth keeping an eye on. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5768866787354642701" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_778871218" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/778871218" />
    <a title="Daphne (Illumicrate)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/365664-daphne-illumicrate"><img alt="Daphne (Illumicrate)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365257777p2/365664.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/778871218?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daphne (Illumicrate)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daphne (Illumicrate)" href="/user/show/365664-daphne-illumicrate">Daphne (Illumicrate)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/365664-daphne-illumicrate?shelf=genre-mystery">genre-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/365664-daphne-illumicrate?shelf=age-ya">age-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/365664-daphne-illumicrate?shelf=type-arc-hardcopy">type-arc-hardcopy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/365664-daphne-illumicrate?shelf=2014-debut-author">2014-debut-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/365664-daphne-illumicrate?shelf=2014-release">2014-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/365664-daphne-illumicrate?shelf=ukmg">ukmg</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer778871218" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2290652752471520272"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>If you put Nancy Drew in a boarding school, set it in the 1930s and sprinkle heavily with Sherlock references, bunbreaks and Cluedo, you’re getting close to describing the sheer charm that is Murder Most Unladylike. I absolutely adored Robin Stevens’ debut novel featuring the first case of the Wells & Wong Detective Society. As a warning, you will definitely want to read this book with a cup of tea and baked goods within arm’s reach. <br/><br/>And if you need more to sell you on this book, there </span>
  <span id="freeText2290652752471520272" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br /><br />If you put Nancy Drew in a boarding school, set it in the 1930s and sprinkle heavily with Sherlock references, bunbreaks and Cluedo, you’re getting close to describing the sheer charm that is Murder Most Unladylike. I absolutely adored Robin Stevens’ debut novel featuring the first case of the Wells &amp; Wong Detective Society. As a warning, you will definitely want to read this book with a cup of tea and baked goods within arm’s reach. <br /><br />And if you need more to sell you on this book, there is a map (!) of the Deepdean School for Girls and a cast list up front so you can follow along as the girls try to convince everyone their teacher was murdered and also solve the whodunit. Plus, the cover is gorgeously blue with striking graphics and typography and would look great on your shelves. It’s hard to pinpoint exactly why I love this book so much but everything about it is simply lovely.<br /><br />The main girls are wonderfully likable and memorable...<br /><br /><b>For more, see full review published at <a href="http://www.wingedreviews.com/2014/07/murder-most-unladylike-robin-stevens/" rel="nofollow noopener">Winged Reviews</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="2290652752471520272" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1004655685" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1004655685" />
    <a title="Emma Rose Ribbons" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3915178-emma-rose-ribbons"><img alt="Emma Rose Ribbons" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557779894p2/3915178.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1004655685?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Rose Ribbons" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Rose Ribbons" href="/user/show/3915178-emma-rose-ribbons">Emma Rose Ribbons</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/20946352-murder-is-bad-manners">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3915178-emma-rose-ribbons?shelf=historical-mystery">historical-mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1004655685" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1799800392110841140">I'd like to add some thoughts after rereading this book. As much as I enjoyed it this time around, I think that I would have liked a little more humour and fun and overall silliness, which I really missed, especially because I think there were plenty of opportunites for that. I'm also not too fond of the resolution because it should have been the girls' detective work throughout. Bringing a professional detective at the end may be realistic, it's a little too much to ask of me to like him when a</span>
  <span id="freeText1799800392110841140" style="display:none">I'd like to add some thoughts after rereading this book. As much as I enjoyed it this time around, I think that I would have liked a little more humour and fun and overall silliness, which I really missed, especially because I think there were plenty of opportunites for that. I'm also not too fond of the resolution because it should have been the girls' detective work throughout. Bringing a professional detective at the end may be realistic, it's a little too much to ask of me to like him when all along girls did the work and he's reaping the rewards.<br />Bottom line: this was a good read with heaps of things to enjoy but I'm also happy it's the first in a series because there's also loads of other things to do with it.<br /><br /><br />This was my original review:<br /><br />CORGI HERE'S A MESSAGE FOR YOU: DON'T YOU DARE NOT PUBLISH THE MANY MANY MANY BOOKS THIS SERIES IS LIKELY TO CONTAIN. THIS WAS TOO DELIGHTFUL AND TOO MUCH WHAT I NEED IN MY LIFE AND TOO MUCH THE BOOK I WISH I'D WRITTEN. SCHOOL MYSTERIES ARE MY DRUG. I WILL HUNT YOU DOWN, CORGI. NO, SERIOUSLY, I WILL! I KNOW YOU'RE READING THIS. THANK YOU ❤</span>
  <a data-text-id="1799800392110841140" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZEFjhR31BSPDHMciRZxIiJTiwiF3eVZYlRmSpFqxu8zkHTH+rEUpiJ90HHepU43uYrAQW5uGK8td8Qq3U/yQEQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nE6Dii4sAuEqBCJy1/GQYIypBatBzWYUJP/nAVIUFSUcEtHxn5wuSnZs+Sc7PlUGevvX0a0yG4fsF38SW1k++A==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15041109609856515342">Robin's books are: Murder Most Unladylike (Murder is Bad Manners in the USA), Arsenic for Tea (Poison is Not Polite in the USA), First Class Murder, Jolly Foul Play, Mistletoe and Murder, Cream Buns and Crime, A Spoonful of Murder, Death in the Spotlight and Top Marks for Murder. She is also the author of The Guggenheim Mystery, the sequel to Siobhan Dowd's The London Eye Mystery. <br/><br/>Robin was born i</span>
  <span id="freeText15041109609856515342" style="display:none">Robin's books are: Murder Most Unladylike (Murder is Bad Manners in the USA), Arsenic for Tea (Poison is Not Polite in the USA), First Class Murder, Jolly Foul Play, Mistletoe and Murder, Cream Buns and Crime, A Spoonful of Murder, Death in the Spotlight and Top Marks for Murder. She is also the author of The Guggenheim Mystery, the sequel to Siobhan Dowd's The London Eye Mystery. <br /><br />Robin was born in California and grew up in an Oxford college, across the road from the house where Alice in Wonderland lived. She has been making up stories all her life.<br /><br />When she was twelve, her father handed her a copy of The Murder of Roger Ackroyd and she realised that she wanted to be either Hercule Poirot or Agatha Christie when she grew up. When it occurred to her that she was never going to be able to grow her own spectacular walrus moustache, she decided that Agatha Christie was the more achieveable option.<br /><br />She spent her teenage years at Cheltenham Ladies’ College, reading a lot of murder mysteries and hoping that she’d get the chance to do some detecting herself (she didn’t). She then went to university, where she studied crime fiction, and then worked at a children's publisher.<br /><br />Robin lives in England with her husband and her pet bearded dragon, Watson.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15041109609856515342" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
